Dear Mr. Wataru: 
In accordance with our fee proposal dated February 26, 2016 with D.R. Horton – 
Schuler Division, we have provided earthwork observation and compaction testing 
services for the Ho’opili Phase 1 – Parcel 1 (Single-Family) project. In general, our 
geotechnical engineering observations during the site grading operations for this project 
were performed from November 30, 2016 through October 4, 2018. The results of our field 
observations and compaction tests are provided in the attached Earthwork Observation 
and Compaction Testing Report dated May 13, 2019. 
I certify that Geolabs performed the earthwork compaction tests. To the best of our 
knowledge, it is our professional opinion that the grading work observed by Geolabs has 
been constructed in general conformance with the approved plans and Standard 
Specifications for Public Works Construction, City & County of Honolulu, and our 
geotechnical report and subsequent recommendations provided for the above project.

EARTHWORK OBSERVATION AND COMPACTION TESTING 
HO’OPILI PHASE 1 – PARCEL 1 (SINGLE-FAMILY) 
EWA, OAHU, HAWAII 
Grading Permit Nos.: GP2016-10-0473, GP2017-10-0495 & GP2018-10-0405 
Dear Ms. Yanagawa: 
We are pleased to submit our geotechnical engineering earthwork observations and 
testing report for work performed during the site grading operation of Ho’opili Phase 1 – 
Parcel 1 (Single-Family) project in general accordance with our fee proposal dated 
February 26, 2016, and subsequent additional budget requests. 
PROJECT CONSIDERATIONS 
The proposed Ho’opili Development project is to the south of the Interstate Route 
H-1 Highway and west of Fort Weaver Road in the Ewa area on the Island of Oahu, Hawaii.
The Ho`opili development encompasses approximately 1,500 acres. The project site is
gently sloping and is currently used for agricultural cultivation.
The Parcel 1 consists of a 103-unit single-family residential subdivision within a 
16.4-acre parcel bordered by Keahumoa Parkway to the north and Ewa Villages Golf 
Course to the south, as shown on the Site Plan, Plate 1. 
The site grading consisted of minor cuts and fills of generally less than 5 feet. Royal 
Contracting Co. Ltd. performed the earthwork operations for the project. 
SITE GRADING 
At the on-set of earthwork, areas within the contract grading limits were generally 
cleared and grubbed of vegetation and deleterious materials. Materials generated from 
the clearing operations were disposed of off-site. Following the clearing and grubbing 
operations, the areas to be cut were excavated. Finished grades were compacted using 
a sheepsfoot and/or smooth vibratory drum roller. It should be noted that the upper 2 feet 
of the subgrade was previously moisture-conditioned to about 2 to 4 percent above the 
Page 2 
D.R. Horton – Schuler Division
W.O. 7015-20(D) (Grading Permit Nos.: GP2016-10-0473, GP2017-10-0495 & GP2018-10-0405) 
May 13, 2019
GEOLABS, INC. 
Hawaii • California
optimum moisture content and compacted to a minimum of 85 to 90 percent of the 
maximum dry density, forming a 2-foot thick rework zone during the mass grading 
operation. 
Soft and yielding areas encountered during clearing and grubbing were generally 
over-excavated to expose firm natural material, and the resulting excavation was backfilled 
with well-compacted engineered fill. 
The fill and backfill materials were moisture-conditioned to above the optimum 
moisture content and compacted to a minimum of 90 percent of the maximum dry density 
as determined in accordance with ASTM D1557.  In the roadway areas, the subgrade 
was capped by 18 inches of select granular fills and compacted to a minimum of 
95 percent of the maximum dry density. 
During the site grading operations, samples of the materials utilized as fill were 
obtained and transported to our laboratory for testing.  The maximum dry densities and 
optimum moisture contents were established in general accordance with ASTM D1557 
(Modified Proctor), and the test results are summarized on Plate 2. 
Periodic in-situ moisture and density tests were conducted in general accordance 
with ASTM D6938 (Nuclear Gauge Method), to determine the adequacy of compaction of 
fills and backfills for infrastructure and utility installations, including compaction of building 
pads, garages, walkways, and driveways.  
The test results are summarized on Plates 3.1 through 3.98. These tests were 
performed on moisture-conditioned and compacted lifts of fills and backfills.  Test 
locations and elevations were estimated using on-site survey stakes for reference.  These 
locations and elevations should be considered accurate only to the degree implied by the 
methods used. Areas deemed unsatisfactory were reworked until the measured relative 
compaction conformed to or exceeded the minimum specified for the project. 
This report summarizes our field observations and compaction testing 
services during the site grading work for the period covering November 30, 2016 to 
October 4, 2018. 
Based on our field representative’s observations and the referenced test results, it 
is our opinion that the site grading for Ho’opili Phase 1 – Parcel 1 (Single-Family) project, 
observed and tested by Geolabs in the period covered by this report, were performed in 
accordance with the general intent of the recommendations in the following references.

LIMITATIONS 
Geolabs assumes no responsibility for alterations made to finished grades on the 
project subsequent to our observation and testing period without our knowledge and 
written acknowledgment. 
It should be noted that it is not possible to continuously observe all activities 
occurring simultaneously on a construction site; therefore, some work may have occurred 
without our observation.  However, we believe the level of earthwork observation and 
testing services provided is reasonable in reducing the geotechnical risks to the project.  
It should be recognized that there are variations in the accuracy and statistical 
repeatability of the tests and methods used to monitor the earthwork construction and 
materials.  Our services were performed in accordance with generally accepted standards 
of geotechnical engineering practice; no warranty is expressed or implied. Provision of 
construction monitoring by an engineer is not insurance, nor does it guarantee 
construction of any type.  The contractor shall retain responsibility for the quality of the 
work, for adhering to the plans and specifications, and for repairing defects regardless of 
when they are found.
